# Investigation: Stale Envoy Route Configuration After DestinationRule Update in Istio

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/istio--f8c9b973 (mirror of istio/istio)
**Task Type:** Deep Causal Chain (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

An Istio service mesh operator reports that updating a DestinationRule in their cluster **silently fails to propagate** to Envoy sidecars. Specifically, when they have multiple DestinationRules for the same host (e.g., one defining subsets, another defining traffic policy), updating one of them does not trigger an xDS push — the Envoy sidecar continues serving the **stale** cluster and route configuration.

The operator has two DestinationRules for `reviews.default.svc.cluster.local`:

**DR-1 (traffic policy):**
```yaml
apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3
kind: DestinationRule
metadata:
  name: reviews-traffic-policy
  namespace: default
spec:
  host: reviews.default.svc.cluster.local
  trafficPolicy:
    connectionPool:
      tcp:
        maxConnections: 100
      http:
        h2UpgradePolicy: UPGRADE
```

**DR-2 (subsets):**
```yaml
apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3
kind: DestinationRule
metadata:
  name: reviews-subsets
  namespace: default
spec:
  host: reviews.default.svc.cluster.local
  subsets:
    - name: v1
      labels:
        version: v1
    - name: v2
      labels:
        version: v2
```

When the operator updates `reviews-subsets` (e.g., adding a `v3` subset), the Envoy sidecar does **not** receive updated CDS/RDS config. Only restarting the pod picks up the change. Updating `reviews-traffic-policy` also has no effect.

Istio debug endpoint `GET /debug/config_dump` on the sidecar shows the old configuration even after the DestinationRule has been updated in the Kubernetes API server.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause of why updating a merged DestinationRule fails to trigger an xDS push, and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:

1. **How Istio merges multiple DestinationRules for the same host** — specifically the `mergeDestinationRule()` function in `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go` and how it combines subsets and traffic policies from multiple DRs into a single merged config
2. **How the merged DestinationRule loses identity metadata** — when two DRs are merged, only one DR's `config.Config` metadata (name/namespace) survives in the `consolidatedDestRules` structure. The metadata of contributing DRs is lost.
3. **How SidecarScope builds config dependencies** — the `AddConfigDependencies()` calls in `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go` that register which config resources a proxy depends on. Specifically, how `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` and `ConvertToSidecarScope()` iterate over `destinationRules` and add `ConfigKey{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: dr.Name, Namespace: dr.Namespace}` for each DR
4. **The specific gap: only one DR's ConfigKey is registered** — because the merged DR has only one name/namespace, `AddConfigDependencies` registers only that one DR. The other contributing DR(s) are not tracked.
5. **How the xDS push filter uses DependsOnConfig** — when a config change event occurs, `pilot/pkg/xds/` calls `SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(configKey)` to decide if the proxy needs a push. If the updated DR is the one whose metadata was lost during merging, `DependsOnConfig` returns `false` and the push is **incorrectly skipped**.
6. **The relationship between PushContext.destinationRule() and the merge pipeline** — how `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` stores the `destinationRuleIndex` and how `destinationRule()` returns the merged config, obscuring the fact that multiple DRs contributed to it

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Causal Chain
<Ordered list: symptom → intermediate hops → root cause>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- The causal chain spans at least 4 packages: `pilot/pkg/model/`, `pilot/pkg/xds/`, `pilot/pkg/networking/core/`, and `pilot/pkg/config/`
- Focus on how the DestinationRule merging in `destination_rule.go` interacts with dependency tracking in `sidecar.go` and push filtering in the xDS layer

Perfect! I've completed a detailed investigation of the Istio bug and written a comprehensive report. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Investigation Complete

I've written a detailed report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` that traces the root cause of stale Envoy configuration when updating merged DestinationRules.

### Key Findings:

**The Bug:** When multiple DestinationRules target the same host (e.g., one with traffic policy, one with subsets), updating either one fails to trigger xDS pushes to Envoy sidecars.

**Root Cause Chain:**
1. **Merging loses metadata** (`destination_rule.go`): When two DRs merge, only the first DR's Name/Namespace is retained in the merged config
2. **Dependencies incomplete** (`sidecar.go`): Only the merged config's metadata is registered in `configDependencies`, not the original DRs'
3. **Push filtering fails** (`proxy_dependencies.go`): When the second DR updates, its ConfigKey hash isn't found in dependencies, so the push is skipped
4. **Obscured origins** (`push_context.go`): The `destinationRule()` lookup returns merged configs, hiding the contributing DRs

**The Specific Gap:** In `destination_rule.go` lines 59-61, when both DRs lack workload selectors, the second DR is merged into the first and NOT appended as a separate entry. This means only one DR's ConfigKey ever gets registered in the dependency tracking system.

**Evidence:** The report provides specific code references showing:
- Lines in destination_rule.go where metadata is lost during deep copy
- Lines in sidecar.go where only the merged config's metadata is registered
- The ConfigKey hash function that prevents finding unregistered DRs
- The proxy_dependencies.go filter that incorrectly skips the push

The investigation spans 4 packages and shows the causal chain f

is a wrapper over the Sidecar resource with some\n56: // preprocessed data to determine the list of services, virtualServices,\n57: // and destinationRules that are accessible to a given\n58: // sidecar. Precomputing the list of services, virtual services, dest rules\n59: // for a sidecar improves performance as we no longer need to compute this\n60: // list for every sidecar. We simply have to match a sidecar to a\n61: // SidecarScope. Note that this is not the same as public/private scoped\n62: // services. The list of services seen by every sidecar scope (namespace\n63: // wide or per workload) depends on the imports, the listeners, and other\n64: // settings.\n65: //\n66: // Every proxy workload of SidecarProxy type will always map to a\n67: // SidecarScope object. Each hostname in this map\n98: \t// corresponds to a service in the services array above. This means we should use the default - either an implicit\n958: \t// default selecting everything, or pulling from the root namespace.\n959: \tps.sidecarIndex.defaultSidecarMu.Lock()\n960: \tdefer ps.sidecarIndex.defaultSidecarMu.Unlock()\n961: \tif proxy.Type == Router {\n962: \t\tsc, f := ps.sidecarIndex.gatewayDefaultSidecarsByNamespace[proxy.ConfigNamespace]\n963: \t\tif f {\n964: \t\t\t// We have already computed the scope for this namespace, just fetch it\n965: \t\t\treturn sc\n966: \t\t}\n967: \t\tcomputed := DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace(ps, proxy.ConfigNamespace)\n968: \t\tps.sidecarIndex.gatewayDefaultSidecarsByNamespace[proxy.ConfigNamespace] = computed\n969: \t\treturn computed\n970: \t}\n971: \tsc, f := ps.sidecarIndex.computedSidecarsByNamespace[proxy.ConfigNamespace]\n972: \tif f {\n973: \t\t// We have already computed the scope for this namespace, just fetch it\n974: \t\treturn sc\n975: \t}\n976: \t// We need to compute this namespace\n977: \tvar computed *SidecarScope\n978: \tif ps.sidecarIndex.rootConfig != nil {\n979: \t\tcomputed = ConvertToSidecarScope(ps, ps.sidecarIndex.rootConfig, proxy.ConfigNamespace)\n980: \t} else {\n981: \t\tcomputed = DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace(ps, proxy.ConfigNamespace)\n982: \t\t// Even though we are a sidecar, we can store this as a gateway one since it could be used by a gateway\n983: \t\tps.sidecarIndex.gatewayDefaultSidecarsByNamespace[proxy.ConfigNamespace] = computed\n984: \t}\n985: \tps.sidecarIndex.computedSidecarsByNamespace[proxy.ConfigNamespace] = computed\n986: \treturn computed\n987: }\n988: \n989: // destinationRule returns a destination rule for a service name in a given namespace.\n990: func (ps *PushContext) destinationRule(proxyNameSpace string, service *Service) []*config.Config {\n991: \tif service == nil {\n992: \t\treturn nil\n993: \t}\n994: \t// If the proxy config namespace is same as the root config namespace\n995: \t// look for dest rules in the service's namespace first. This hack is needed\n996: \t// because sometimes, istio-system tends to become the root config namespace.\n997: \t// Destination rules are defined here for global purposes. We do not want these\n998: \t// catch all destination rules to be the only dest rule, when processing CDS for\n999: \t// proxies like the istio-ingressgateway or istio-egressgateway.\n1000: \t// If there are no service specific dest rules, we will end up picking up the same\n1001: \t// rules anyway, later in the code\n1002: \n1003: \t// 1. select destination rule from proxy config namespace\n1004: \tif proxyNameSpace != ps.Mesh.RootNamespace {\n1005: \t\t// search through the DestinationRules in proxy's namespace first\n1006: \t\tif ps.destinationRuleIndex.namespaceLocal[proxyNameSpace] != nil {\n1007: \t\t\tif hostname, ok := MostSpecificHostMatch(service.Hostname,\n1008: \t\t\t\tps.destinationRuleIndex.namespaceLocal[proxyNameSpace].destRules,\n1009: \t\t\t); ok {\n1010: \t\t\t\treturn ps.destinationRuleIndex.namespaceLocal[proxyNameSpace].destRules[hostname]\n1011: \t\t\t}\n1012: \t\t}\n1013: \t} else {\n1014: \t\t// If this is a namespace local DR in the same namespace, this must be meant for this proxy, so we do not\n1015: \t\t// need to worry about overriding other DRs with *.local type rules here. If we ignore this, then exportTo=. in\n1016: \t\t// root namespace would always be ignored\n1017: \t\tif hostname, ok := MostSpecificHostMatch(service.Hostname,\n1018: \t\t\tps.destinationRuleIndex.rootNamespaceLocal.destRules,\n1019: \t\t); ok {\n1020: \t\t\treturn ps.destinationRuleIndex.rootNamespaceLocal.destRules[hostname]\n1021: \t\t}\n1022: \t}\n1023: \n1024: \t// 2. select destination rule from service namespace\n1025: \tsvcNs := service.Attributes.Namespace\n1026: \n1027: \t// This can happen when finding the subset labels for a proxy in root namespace.\n1028: \t// Because based on a pure cluster's fqdn, we do not know the service and\n1029: \t// construct a fake service without setting Attributes at all.\n1030: \tif svcNs == \"\" {\n1031: \t\tfor _, svc := range ps.servicesExportedToNamespace(proxyNameSpace) {\n1032: \t\t\tif service.Hostname == svc.Hostname && svc.Attributes.Namespace != \"\" {\n1033: \t\t\t\tsvcNs = svc.Attributes.Namespace\n1034: \t\t\t\tbreak\n1035: \t\t\t}\n1036: \t\t}\n1037: \t}\n1038: \n1039: \t// 3. if no private/public rule matched in the calling proxy's namespace,\n1040: \t// check the target service's namespace for exported rules\n1041: \tif svcNs != \"\" {\n1042: \t\tif out := ps.getExportedDestinationRuleFromNamespace(svcNs, service.Hostname, proxyNameSpace); out != nil {\n1043: \t\t\treturn out\n1044: \t\t}\n1045: \t}\n1046: \n1047: \t// 4. if no public/private rule in calling proxy's namespace matched, and no public rule in the\n1048: \t// target service's namespace matched, search for any exported destination rule in the config root namespace\n1049: \tif out := ps.getExportedDestinationRuleFromNamespace(ps.Mesh.RootNamespace, service.Hostname, proxyNameSpace); out != nil {\n1050: \t\treturn out\n1051: \t}\n1052: \n1053: \t// 5. service DestinationRules were merged in SetDestinationRules, return mesh/namespace rules if present\n1054: \tif features.EnableDestinationRuleInheritance {\n1055: \t\t// return namespace rule if present\n1056: \t\tif out := ps.destinationRuleIndex.inheritedByNamespace[proxyNameSpace];   "content": "# Investigation Report: Stale Envoy Route Configuration After DestinationRule Update in Istio\n\n## Summary\nWhen multiple DestinationRules exist for the same host in Istio, updating one of them fails to trigger an xDS push to Envoy sidecars. This occurs because the merging process loses the identity metadata of contributing DestinationRules, causing the dependency tracking system to miss configuration changes on those DRs.\n\n## Root Cause\nThe root cause spans four interconnected layers:\n\n1. **DestinationRule Merging (destination_rule.go)**: Multiple DRs targeting the same FQDN host are merged into a single config that combines their subsets and traffic policies, but **only one DR's metadata (Name/Namespace) is retained** in the merged config.\n\n2. **Dependency Tracking Loss (sidecar.go)**: When SidecarScope builds its config dependencies, it only registers the metadata from the merged config's Name/Namespace fields, completely losing track of the other contributing DRs.\n\n3. **Push Filtering (proxy_dependencies.go)**: When a config update occurs, the xDS layer checks if a proxy depends on that config using `DependsOnConfig()`, which fails if the updated DR's metadata was lost during merging.\n\n4. **Metadata Obscuration (push_context.go)**: The `destinationRule()` method returns the merged config from the index, making it impossible for downstream code to know which DRs contributed to it.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. Merging Process Loses Metadata\n**File: `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`**\n\nThe `mergeDestinationRule()` function merges multiple DRs for the same host:\n- Lines 41-104: When a DR for the same host already exists, it enters the merge logic\n- Line 65-66: Deep copies the first DR and stores it back at index i\n- Lines 77-87: Appends subsets from the incoming DR to the copied first DR\n- **Critical**: The deep copied first DR retains **its original metadata (Name/Namespace)**, not the incoming DR's metadata\n- Line 59-61: When both DRs have no workload selector, `addRuleToProcessedDestRules = false`\n- **Result**: The second DR is NOT appended as a separate entry; it's merged into the first DR, losing its identity\n\n### 2. Dependency Registration Only Captures One DR's Metadata\n**File: `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:219-227` and `410-416`**\n\nWhen building SidecarScope, the code iterates through destination rules:\n\n```go\n// Lines 219-227 in DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace\nfor _, drList := range out.destinationRules {\n    for _, dr := range drList {\n        out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n            Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n            Name:      dr.Name,           // \u2190 Uses ONLY merged config's metadata\n            Namespace: dr.Namespace,      // \u2190 Other DRs' metadata is lost\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe same pattern appears in `ConvertToSidecarScope()` at lines 410-416.\n\nFor the scenario with two DRs (reviews-traffic-policy and reviews-subsets):\n- If reviews-traffic-policy is created first, it gets merged into\n- When reviews-subsets arrives, it's merged into the first DR\n- **Only** `ConfigKey{Name: \"reviews-traffic-policy\", Namespace: \"default\"}` is registered\n- **Never** `ConfigKey{Name: \"reviews-subsets\", Namespace: \"default\"}`\n\n### 3. Push Filtering Fails to Match Merged DRs\n**File: `pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go:32-74`**\n\nWhen a config update event occurs:\n\n```go\n// Line 52: Calls checkProxyDependencies for each updated config\nif affected && checkProxyDependencies(proxy, config) {\n    return true\n}\n\n// Lines 60-68: checkProxyDependencies\nfunc checkProxyDependencies(proxy *model.Proxy, config model.ConfigKey) bool {\n    switch proxy.Type {\n    case model.SidecarProxy:\n        if proxy.SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(config) {  // \u2190 Checks dependency\n            return true\n        }\n    }\n    return false\n}\n```\n\nIf `config` is `{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: \"reviews-subsets\", Namespace: \"default\"}`, but only `\"reviews-traffic-policy\"` is registered in `configDependencies`, this returns **false** and the push is skipped.\n\n### 4. DependsOnConfig Uses Hash-Based Lookup\n**File: `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:521-540` and `pilot/pkg/model/config.go:60-74`**\n\nThe `DependsOnConfig()` method checks if a config is in the dependency map:\n\n```go\n// pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:538\n_, exists := sc.configDependencies[config.HashCode()]\nreturn exists\n\n// pilot/pkg/model/config.go:60-74\nfunc (key ConfigKey) HashCode() uint64 {\n    hash := md5.New()\n    for _, v := range []string{\n        key.Name,        // \u2190 Hash includes Name\n        key.Namespace,   // \u2190 Hash includes Namespace\n        key.Kind.Kind,\n        key.Kind.Group,\n        key.Kind.Version,\n    } {\n        hash.Write([]byte(v))\n    }\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nSince the hash is computed from Name and Namespace, an updated DR with a different Name than what was registered will have a different hash and won't be found.\n\n### 5. PushContext.destinationRule() Obscures Merged Origins\n**File: `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:989-1066`**\n\nThe `destinationRule()` method returns configs from the `destinationRuleIndex`, which was populated by `SetDestinationRules()` that called `mergeDestinationRule()`:\n\n- Lines 1006-1010: Returns `ps.destinationRuleIndex.namespaceLocal[...].destRules[hostname]`\n- This returns the **merged config(s)**, with only the first DR's metadata\n\nCallers cannot determine that multiple DRs contributed to the merged result.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go**: Implements the merging logic that loses metadata\n2. **pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go**: Builds the destinationRuleIndex and provides `destinationRule()` lookup\n3. **pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go**: Builds SidecarScope and registers config dependencies\n4. **pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go**: Filters xDS pushes based on dependency checking\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Symptom**: Updating a DestinationRule (e.g., reviews-subsets) produces no xDS update to proxies\n2. **\u2192 Push filtering skips the proxy**: `ConfigAffectsProxy()` returns false for the updated DR\n3. **\u2192 Dependency lookup fails**: `checkProxyDependencies()` calls `DependsOnConfig()` which returns false\n4. **\u2192 Updated DR not in dependency map**: Only the first DR's metadata was registered in `configDependencies`\n5. **\u2192 Merged config loses second DR's metadata**: During `mergeDestinationRule()`, the second DR is merged into the first without appending as a separate entry\n6. **\u2192 Only first DR's metadata retained**: The deep-copied merged config at lines 65-66 keeps only the first DR's Name/Namespace\n7. **\u2192 Root cause**: When both DRs lack workload selectors, `addRuleToProcessedDestRules` is set to false (line 59-61), preventing the second DR from being tracked as a separate entity\n\n## Affected Code Flow\n\n```\nSetDestinationRules() [push_context.go:1672]\n    \u2193\nmergeDestinationRule() [destination_rule.go:38]\n    \u2193 (for 2nd DR with same host, no workload selector)\n    \u2193 bothWithoutSelector=true \u2192 addRuleToProcessedDestRules=false\n    \u2193 Merges subsets into first DR, keeps first DR's metadata\n    \u2193 Returns WITHOUT appending second DR\n    \u2193\ndestinationRuleIndex populated with merged config [only first DR's Name/Namespace]\n    \u2193\nDefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace() / ConvertToSidecarScope() [sidecar.go]\n    \u2193\nIterates destinationRules and calls AddConfigDependencies()\n    \u2193 Registers ONLY first DR's ConfigKey\n    \u2193\nProxyDependencies.checkProxyDependencies()\n    \u2193 (when second DR is updated)\n    \u2193 Calls DependsOnConfig(second_DR's_ConfigKey)\n    \u2193 Second DR's ConfigKey hash NOT in configDependencies\n    \u2193\nPush is SKIPPED, Envoy remains with stale config\n```\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe root cause must be addressed at the dependency tracking level. Possible approaches:\n\n1. **Track All Contributing DRs**: Modify `consolidatedDestRules` to maintain a list of all contributing DR metadata, not just the merged config's metadata. Register all of them in `configDependencies`.\n\n2. **Separate Metadata Storage**: Create a side-map that tracks which original DRs were merged into each merged config, then during dependency registration, register all contributing DRs.\n\n3. **Prevent Merging for Cross-DR Updates**: Only merge DRs if they are guaranteed to always be updated together (unlikely).\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo verify this bug in a cluster:\n\n1. Create two DestinationRules for the same host (e.g., one with traffic policy, one with subsets)\n2. Apply both to the cluster\n3. Check the pilot xDS cache: Use `/debug/config_dump` on a sidecar to confirm merged config\n4. Update the second DR (add a new subset)\n5. Verify sidecar config dump is NOT updated (stale config)\n6. Check pilot logs for config updates - should show the DR was processed\n7. Enable pilot debug logging for `proxy_dependencies` to see `DependsOnConfig()` returning false for the second DR\n\n### Key Insight\n\nThe bug occurs at the intersection of three systems:\n- **Merging**: Consolidates multiple DRs but loses identity\n- **Dependency Tracking**: Only tracks the merged identity\n- **Push Filtering**: Uses ConfigKeys to match changes to tracked dependencies\n\nThe disconnect happens because `mergeDestinationRule()` assumes that only one DR's metadata will be tracked, but in reality, users can independently update any of the contributing DRs at any time.\n",
  "file_path": "/logs/agent/investigation.md"
}

Fix Strategy\n\nThe root cause must be addressed at the dependency tracking level. Possible approaches:\n\n1. **Track All Contributing DRs**: Modify `consolidatedDestRules` to maintain a list of all contributing DR metadata, not just the merged config's metadata. Register all of them in `configDependencies`.\n\n2. **Separate Metadata Storage**: Create a side-map that tracks which original DRs were merged into each merged config, then during dependency registration, register all contributing DRs.\n\n3. **Prevent Merging for Cross-DR Updates**: Only merge DRs if they are guaranteed to always be updated together (unlikely).\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo verify this bug in a cluster:\n\n1. Create two DestinationRules for the same host (e.g., one with traffic policy, one with subsets)\n2. Apply both to the cluster\n3. Check the pilot xDS cache: Use `/debug/config_dump` on a sidecar to confirm merged config\n4. Update the second DR (add a new subset)\n5. Verify sidecar config dump is NOT updated (stale config)\n6. Check pilot logs for config updates - should show the DR was processed\n7. Enable pilot debug logging for `proxy_dependencies` to see `DependsOnConfig()` returning false for the second DR\n\n### Key Insight\n\nThe bug occurs at the intersection of three systems:\n- **Merging**: Consolidates multiple DRs but loses identity\n- **Dependency Tracking**: Only tracks the merged identity\n- **Push Filtering**: Uses ConfigKeys to match changes to tracked dependencies\n\nThe disconnect happens because `mergeDestinationRule()` assumes that only one DR's metadata will be tracked, but in reality, users can independently update any of the contributing DRs at any time.\n",

# Investigation Report: Stale Envoy Route Configuration After DestinationRule Update in Istio

## Summary
When multiple DestinationRules exist for the same host in Istio, updating one of them fails to trigger an xDS push to Envoy sidecars. This occurs because the merging process loses the identity metadata of contributing DestinationRules, causing the dependency tracking system to miss configuration changes on those DRs.

## Root Cause
The root cause spans four interconnected layers:

1. **DestinationRule Merging (destination_rule.go)**: Multiple DRs targeting the same FQDN host are merged into a single config that combines their subsets and traffic policies, but **only one DR's metadata (Name/Namespace) is retained** in the merged config.

2. **Dependency Tracking Loss (sidecar.go)**: When SidecarScope builds its config dependencies, it only registers the metadata from the merged config's Name/Namespace fields, completely losing track of the other contributing DRs.

3. **Push Filtering (proxy_dependencies.go)**: When a config update occurs, the xDS layer checks if a proxy depends on that config using `DependsOnConfig()`, which fails if the updated DR's metadata was lost during merging.

4. **Metadata Obscuration (push_context.go)**: The `destinationRule()` method returns the merged config from the index, making it impossible for downstream code to know which DRs contributed to it.

## Evidence

### 1. Merging Process Loses Metadata
**File: `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`**

The `mergeDestinationRule()` function merges multiple DRs for the same host:
- Lines 41-104: When a DR for the same host already exists, it enters the merge logic
- Line 65-66: Deep copies the first DR and stores it back at index i
- Lines 77-87: Appends subsets from the incoming DR to 
... (truncated)
